help std
 <strong>std</strong> Standard deviation.
    For vectors, Y = <strong>std</strong>(X) returns the standard deviation.  For matrices,
    Y is a row vector containing the standard deviation of each column.  For
    N-D arrays, <strong>std</strong> operates along the first non-singleton dimension of X.
 
    <strong>std</strong> normalizes Y by N-1 if N>1, where N is the sample size.  This is
    the sqrt of an unbiased estimator of the variance of the population
    from which X is drawn, as long as X consists of independent,
    identically distributed samples. For N=1, Y is normalized by N.
 
    Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,1) normalizes by N and produces the square root of the second
    moment of the sample about its mean.  <strong>std</strong>(X,0) is the same as <strong>std</strong>(X).
 
    Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,W) computes the standard deviation using the weight vector W.
    W typically contains either counts or inverse variances.  The length of
    W must equal the length of the dimension over which <strong>std</strong> operates, and
    its elements must be nonnegative.  If X(I) is assumed to have standard
    deviation proportional to 1/SQRT(W(I)), then Y * SQRT(MEAN(W)/W(I)) is
    an estimate of the standard deviation of X(I).  In other words, Y *
    SQRT(MEAN(W)) is an estimate of standard deviation for an observation
    given weight 1.
 
    Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,0,"all") or Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,1,"all") returns the standard deviation
    of all elements of X. A weight of 0 normalizes by N-1 and a weight of 1 
    normalizes by N.
 
    Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,W,DIM) takes the standard deviation along the dimension DIM
    of X.
 
    Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,0,VECDIM) or Y = <strong>std</strong>(X,1,VECDIM) operates on the dimensions 
    specified in the vector VECDIM. A weight of 0 normalizes by N-1 and a 
    weight of 1 normalizes by N. For example, <strong>std</strong>(X,0,[1 2]) operates on
    the elements contained in the first and second dimensions of X.
 
    [Y,M] = <strong>std</strong>(X,...) also returns the mean M of the values in X that 
    was used to calculate the standard deviation. If Y is the weighted
    standard deviation, then M is the weighted mean.
 
    The standard deviation is the square root of the variance (VAR).
 
    <strong>std</strong>(...,NANFLAG) specifies how NaN values are treated:
 
    "includemissing" / "includenan" -
                   (default) The standard deviation of a vector containing
                   NaN values is also NaN.
    "omitmissing" / "omitnan"       -
                   Elements of X or W containing NaN values are ignored.
                   If all elements are NaN, the result is NaN.
 
    Example: 
        X = [4 -2 1; 9 5 7]
        std(X,0,1)
        std(X,0,2)
 
    Class support for inputs X, W:
       float: double, single
 
    See also <a href="matlab:help cov -displayBanner">cov</a>, <a href="matlab:help mean -displayBanner">mean</a>, <a href="matlab:help var -displayBanner">var</a>, <a href="matlab:help median -displayBanner">median</a>, <a href="matlab:help corrcoef -displayBanner">corrcoef</a>.

    <a href="matlab:doc std">Documentation for std</a>
    <a href="matlab:matlab.internal.language.introspective.overloads.displayOverloads('std')">Other uses of std</a>

% Calculate the standard deviation
std_deviation = std(closestDistances,0,'all','omitnan');
